<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>
<s> from the fly arthur sprang out then to the hall door where he was met by a domestic whom he did not know <\s>
<s> the man seemed to be surprised at the approach of the gentleman with the carpet bag which he made no attempt to take from arthur's hands <\s>
<s> her ladyship's not at home sir the man remarked <\s>

<s> take the bag to a dressing room if you please and passing by the porter he walked straight towards that apartment from which as the door opened a warble of melodious notes issued <\s>
<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>
<s> from the fly arthur sprang out then to the hall door where he was met by a domestic whom he did not know <\s>
<s> the man seemed to be surprised at the approach of the gentleman with the carpet bag which he made no attempt to take from arthur's hands <\s>
<s> her ladyship's not at home sir the man remarked <\s>
<s> lightfoot is gone answered the man <\s>
<s> my lady is out and my orders was i hear miss amory's voice in the drawing room said arthur <\s>
<s> take the bag to a dressing room if you please and passing by the porter he walked straight towards that apartment from which as the door opened a warble of melodious notes issued <\s>
<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>

<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>

<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>
<s> from the fly arthur sprang out then to the hall door where he was met by a domestic whom he did not know <\s>
<s> the man seemed to be surprised at the approach of the gentleman with the carpet bag which he made no attempt to take from arthur's hands <\s>
<s> her ladyship's not at home sir the man remarked <\s>
<s> lightfoot is gone answered the man <\s>
<s> my lady is out and my orders was i hear miss amory's voice in the drawing room said arthur <\s>
<s> take the bag to a dressing room if you please and passing by the porter he walked straight towards that apartment from which as the door opened a warble of melodious notes issued <\s>
<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>
<s> as the door opened the gentleman started up with hullo <\s>
<s> the music stopped with a little shriek from the singer frank clavering woke up from the sofa and arthur came forward and said what foker <\s>
<s> how do you do foker <\s>
<s> he looked at the piano and there by miss amory's side was just such another purple leather box as he had seen in harry's hand three days before when the heir of logwood was coming out of a jeweller's shop in waterloo place <\s>
<s> it was opened and curled round the white satin cushion within was oh such a magnificent serpentine bracelet with such a blazing ruby head and diamond tail <\s>
<s> blanche made many motions of the shoulders and gave signs of unrest and agitation <\s>
<s> and she put her handkerchief over the bracelet and then she advanced with a hand which trembled very much to greet pen <\s>
<s> how is dearest laura <\s>
<s> the face of foker looking up from his profound mourning that face so piteous and puzzled was one which the reader's imagination must depict for himself also that of master frank clavering who looking at the three interesting individuals with an expression of the utmost knowingness had only time to ejaculate the words here's a jolly go <\s>
<s> and to disappear sniggering <\s>
<s> pen too had restrained himself up to that minute but looking still at foker whose ears and cheeks tingled with blushes arthur burst out into a fit of laughter so wild and loud that it frightened blanche much more than any the most serious exhibition <\s>
<s> and this was the secret was it <\s>
<s> don't blush and turn away foker my boy <\s>
<s> why man you are a pattern of fidelity <\s>
<s> could i stand between blanche and such constancy could i stand between miss amory and fifteen thousand a year <\s>
<s> it is not that mr <\s>
<s> pendennis blanche said with great dignity <\s>
<s> it is not money it is not rank it is not gold that moves me but it is constancy it is fidelity it is a whole trustful loving heart offered to me that i treasure yes that i treasure <\s>
<s> and she made for her handkerchief but reflecting what was underneath it she paused <\s>
<s> i do not disown i do not disguise my life is above disguise to him on whom it is bestowed my heart must be for ever bare that i once thought i loved you yes thought i was beloved by you i own <\s>
<s> how i clung to that faith <\s>
<s> how i strove i prayed i longed to believe it <\s>
<s> but your conduct always your own words so cold so heartless so unkind have undeceived me <\s>
<s> you trifled with the heart of the poor maiden <\s>
<s> you flung me back with scorn the troth which i had plighted <\s>
<s> i have explained all all to mr <\s>
<s> that you have said foker with devotion and conviction in his looks <\s>
<s> said pen with a meaning look at blanche <\s>
<s> it is i am in fault is it <\s>
<s> well well blanche be it so <\s>
<s> i won't appeal against your sentence and bear it in silence <\s>
<s> i came down here looking to very different things heaven knows and with a heart most truly and kindly disposed towards you <\s>
<s> i hope you may be happy with another as on my word it was my wish to make you so and i hope my honest old friend here will have a wife worthy of his loyalty his constancy and affection <\s>
<s> indeed they deserve the regard of any woman even miss blanche amory <\s>
<s> shake hands harry don't look askance at me <\s>
<s> has anybody told you that i was a false and heartless character <\s>
<s> i think you're a foker was beginning in his wrath when blanche interposed <\s>
<s> henry not a word i pray you let there be forgiveness <\s>
<s> you're an angel by jove you're an angel <\s>
<s> said foker at which blanche looked seraphically up to the chandelier <\s>
<s> in spite of what has passed for the sake of what has passed i must always regard arthur as a brother the seraph continued we have known each other years we have trodden the same fields and plucked the same flowers together <\s>
<s> i beseech you to take hands and to be friends <\s>
<s> forgive you i forgive you arthur with my heart i do <\s>
<s> should i not do so for making me so happy <\s>
<s> there is only one person of us three whom i pity blanche arthur said gravely and i say to you again that i hope you will make this good fellow this honest and loyal creature happy <\s>
<s> at last she said tunbridge wells is not very far off is it arthur <\s>
<s> hadn't you better go and see her <\s>
<s> they had been in town a week and neither had thought of that simple plan before <\s>
<s> shows how arthur had better have taken a return ticket the train carried arthur only too quickly to tunbridge though he had time to review all the circumstances of his life as he made the brief journey and to acknowledge to what sad conclusions his selfishness and waywardness had led him <\s>
<s> here is the end of hopes and aspirations thought he of romance and ambitions <\s>
<s> where i yield or where i am obstinate i am alike unfortunate my mother implores me and i refuse an angel <\s>
<s> say i had taken her forced on me as she was laura would never have been an angel to me <\s>
<s> i could not have given her my heart at another's instigation i never could have known her as she is had i been obliged to ask another to interpret her qualities and point out her virtues <\s>
<s> i yield to my uncle's solicitations and accept on his guarantee blanche and a seat in parliament and wealth and ambition and a career and see fortune comes and leaves me the wife without the dowry which i had taken in compensation of a heart <\s>
<s> why was i not more honest or am i not less so <\s>
<s> it would have cost my poor old uncle no pangs to accept blanche's fortune whencesoever it came he can't even understand he is bitterly indignant heart stricken almost at the scruples which actuate me in refusing it <\s>
<s> a maimed weak imperfect wretch it seems as if i am unequal to any fortune <\s>
<s> i neither make myself nor any one connected with me happy <\s>
<s> what prospect is there for this poor little frivolous girl who is to take my obscure name and share my fortune <\s>
<s> i have not even ambition to excite me or self esteem enough to console myself much more her for my failure <\s>
<s> if i were to write a book that should go through twenty editions why i should be the very first to sneer at my reputation <\s>
<s> say i could succeed at the bar and achieve a fortune by bullying witnesses and twisting evidence is that a fame which would satisfy my longings or a calling in which my life would be well spent <\s>
<s> how i wish i could be that priest opposite who never has lifted his eyes from his breviary except when we were in reigate tunnel when he could not see or that old gentleman next him who scowls at him with eyes of hatred over his newspaper <\s>
<s> the priest shuts his eyes to the world but has his thoughts on the book which is his directory to the world to come <\s>
<s> his neighbour hates him as a monster tyrant persecutor and fancies burning martyrs and that pale countenance looking on and lighted up by the flame <\s>
<s> these have no doubts these march on trustfully bearing their load of logic <\s>
<s> would you like to look at the paper sir <\s>
<s> here interposed the stout gentleman it had a flaming article against the order of the black coated gentleman who was travelling with them in the carriage and pen thanked him and took it and pursued his reverie without reading two sentences of the journal <\s>
<s> and yet would you take either of those men's creeds with its consequences <\s>
<s> you must bear your own burthen fashion your own faith think your own thoughts and pray your own prayer <\s>
<s> to what mortal ear could i tell all if i had a mind <\s>
<s> or who could understand all <\s>
<s> who can tell another's shortcomings lost opportunities weigh the passions which overpower the defects which incapacitate reason what extent of truth and right his neighbour's mind is organised to perceive and to do what invisible and forgotten accident terror of youth chance or mischance of fortune may have altered the whole current of life <\s>
<s> a grain of sand may alter it as the flinging of a pebble may end it <\s>
<s> who can weigh circumstances passions temptations that go to our good and evil account save one before whose awful wisdom we kneel and at whose mercy we ask absolution <\s>
<s> here it ends thought pen this day or to morrow will wind up the account of my youth a weary retrospect alas <\s>
<s> a sad history with many a page i would fain not look back on <\s>
<s> but who has not been tired or fallen and who has escaped without scars from that struggle <\s>
<s> and his head fell on his breast and the young man's heart prostrated itself humbly and sadly before that throne where sits wisdom and love and pity for all and made its confession <\s>
<s> what matters about fame or poverty <\s>
<s> if i marry this woman i have chosen may i have strength and will to be true to her and to make her happy <\s>
<s> if i have children pray god teach me to speak and to do the truth among them and to leave them an honest name <\s>
<s> there are no splendours for my marriage <\s>
<s> does my life deserve any <\s>

<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>
<s> as the door opened the gentleman started up with hullo <\s>

<s> blanche made many motions of the shoulders and gave signs of unrest and agitation <\s>

<s> they had been in town a week and neither had thought of that simple plan before <\s>
<s> shows how arthur had better have taken a return ticket the train carried arthur only too quickly to tunbridge though he had time to review all the circumstances of his life as he made the brief journey and to acknowledge to what sad conclusions his selfishness and waywardness had led him <\s>
<s> here is the end of hopes and aspirations thought he of romance and ambitions <\s>
<s> where i yield or where i am obstinate i am alike unfortunate my mother implores me and i refuse an angel <\s>
<s> say i had taken her forced on me as she was laura would never have been an angel to me <\s>
<s> i could not have given her my heart at another's instigation i never could have known her as she is had i been obliged to ask another to interpret her qualities and point out her virtues <\s>
<s> i yield to my uncle's solicitations and accept on his guarantee blanche and a seat in parliament and wealth and ambition and a career and see fortune comes and leaves me the wife without the dowry which i had taken in compensation of a heart <\s>
<s> why was i not more honest or am i not less so <\s>
<s> it would have cost my poor old uncle no pangs to accept blanche's fortune whencesoever it came he can't even understand he is bitterly indignant heart stricken almost at the scruples which actuate me in refusing it <\s>

<s> i neither make myself nor any one connected with me happy <\s>
<s> what prospect is there for this poor little frivolous girl who is to take my obscure name and share my fortune <\s>
<s> i have not even ambition to excite me or self esteem enough to console myself much more her for my failure <\s>
<s> if i were to write a book that should go through twenty editions why i should be the very first to sneer at my reputation <\s>
<s> say i could succeed at the bar and achieve a fortune by bullying witnesses and twisting evidence is that a fame which would satisfy my longings or a calling in which my life would be well spent <\s>
<s> how i wish i could be that priest opposite who never has lifted his eyes from his breviary except when we were in reigate tunnel when he could not see or that old gentleman next him who scowls at him with eyes of hatred over his newspaper <\s>
<s> the priest shuts his eyes to the world but has his thoughts on the book which is his directory to the world to come <\s>
<s> his neighbour hates him as a monster tyrant persecutor and fancies burning martyrs and that pale countenance looking on and lighted up by the flame <\s>
<s> these have no doubts these march on trustfully bearing their load of logic <\s>
<s> would you like to look at the paper sir <\s>
<s> here interposed the stout gentleman it had a flaming article against the order of the black coated gentleman who was travelling with them in the carriage and pen thanked him and took it and pursued his reverie without reading two sentences of the journal <\s>
<s> and yet would you take either of those men's creeds with its consequences <\s>
<s> you must bear your own burthen fashion your own faith think your own thoughts and pray your own prayer <\s>
<s> to what mortal ear could i tell all if i had a mind <\s>
<s> or who could understand all <\s>
<s> who can tell another's shortcomings lost opportunities weigh the passions which overpower the defects which incapacitate reason what extent of truth and right his neighbour's mind is organised to perceive and to do what invisible and forgotten accident terror of youth chance or mischance of fortune may have altered the whole current of life <\s>
<s> a grain of sand may alter it as the flinging of a pebble may end it <\s>

<s> here it ends thought pen this day or to morrow will wind up the account of my youth a weary retrospect alas <\s>
<s> a sad history with many a page i would fain not look back on <\s>
<s> but who has not been tired or fallen and who has escaped without scars from that struggle <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>
<s> from the fly arthur sprang out then to the hall door where he was met by a domestic whom he did not know <\s>
<s> the man seemed to be surprised at the approach of the gentleman with the carpet bag which he made no attempt to take from arthur's hands <\s>

<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>

<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
<s> let smirke be called in and let us be married out of hand and with all my heart i purpose to keep my vow and to cherish you through life and to be a true and a loving husband to you <\s>
<s> from the fly arthur sprang out then to the hall door where he was met by a domestic whom he did not know <\s>
<s> the man seemed to be surprised at the approach of the gentleman with the carpet bag which he made no attempt to take from arthur's hands <\s>
<s> her ladyship's not at home sir the man remarked <\s>
<s> lightfoot is gone answered the man <\s>
<s> my lady is out and my orders was i hear miss amory's voice in the drawing room said arthur <\s>
<s> take the bag to a dressing room if you please and passing by the porter he walked straight towards that apartment from which as the door opened a warble of melodious notes issued <\s>
<s> our little siren was at her piano singing with all her might and fascinations <\s>
<s> master clavering was asleep on the sofa indifferent to the music but near blanche sat a gentleman who was perfectly enraptured with her strain which was of a passionate and melancholy nature <\s>
<s> as the door opened the gentleman started up with hullo <\s>

<s> the train stopped at tunbridge as pen was making these reflections and he handed over the newspaper to his neighbour of whom he took leave while the foreign clergyman in the opposite corner still sate with his eyes on his book <\s>
<s> pen jumped out of the carriage then his carpet bag in hand and briskly determined to face his fortune <\s>
<s> a fly carried him rapidly to lady clavering's house from the station and as he was transported thither arthur composed a little speech which he intended to address to blanche and which was really as virtuous honest and well minded an oration as any man of his turn of mind and under his circumstances could have uttered <\s>
<s> the purport of it was blanche i cannot understand from your last letter what your meaning is or whether my fair and frank proposal to you is acceptable or no <\s>
<s> i think you know the reason which induces me to forgo the worldly advantages which a union with you offered and which i could not accept without as i fancy being dishonoured <\s>
<s> if you doubt of my affection here i am ready to prove it <\s>
